  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a5bfa48-8c24-4123-af20-10e1c3dff920'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_2364227513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2364227513" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2364227513?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2364227513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8385616232460863617"><b>I really think Wonka needs to stick with his Chocolate Factory...</b><br/><br/>Maybe it's just me...but this one just <b>didn't have the same spark</b> as Charlie and the Chocolate Factory.<blockquote>
  <i>“Hooray!" said the Chief of the Army. "Let's blow everyone up! Bang-bang! Bang-bang!” </i>
</blockquote> We last left Charlie and his family soaring up into the sky in the great glass elevator. They're about to start their <b>next big adventure, </b>with their feet firmly planted in the sky.<br/><br/>Physics aside, the Bucket Family and Willy Wonka putter aroun</span>
  <span id="freeText8385616232460863617" style="display:none"><b>I really think Wonka needs to stick with his Chocolate Factory...</b><br /><br />Maybe it's just me...but this one just <b>didn't have the same spark</b> as Charlie and the Chocolate Factory.<blockquote>
  <i>“Hooray!" said the Chief of the Army. "Let's blow everyone up! Bang-bang! Bang-bang!” </i>
</blockquote> We last left Charlie and his family soaring up into the sky in the great glass elevator. They're about to start their <b>next big adventure, </b>with their feet firmly planted in the sky.<br /><br />Physics aside, the Bucket Family and Willy Wonka putter around rather amusingly until they spot a <b>space station hotel.</b><blockquote>
  <i>My Great Glass Elevator is ready for anything! In we go! Into the breach, dear friends, into the breach!</i>
</blockquote>The moment they set foot into the station, <b>all heck breaks loose</b>. I didn't know where to look. Between Charlie, Mr. Wonka, his parents and all four of his grandparents, there was surely enough <b>misadventures</b> to keep even the most restless of children entertained. <blockquote>
  <i>A little nonsense now and then, is relished by the wisest men,” Mr. Wonka said.</i>
</blockquote> Overall, this was <b>an interesting one. </b>I certainly couldn't have predicted where this was going but was pleasantly surprised by the ending. <br /><br />That being said, I was really disappointed that this one was so paled so much in comparison with the first novel. There was no naughty kids getting their<b> just deserts, </b>there weren't any <b>creepily cheerful </b>Oompa-Loompa songs and (most importantly) <b>hardly any chocolate factory.</b><br /><br />I don't think I'll be going for a reread any time soon.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Really enjoyed all of the inflections and tones. Certainly made this one fun to listen to! Douglas Hodge certainly knew what he was doing when he read this one!<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8385616232460863617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616246920?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JV (semi-hiatus)" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus">JV (semi-hiatus)</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410325" href="/book/show/109073.Charlie_and_the_Great_Glass_Elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=2018">2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616246920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16187621979243165065"><b>[Preflight Announcement]</b><br/><br/>Good day, ladies and gentlemen! <br/>Welcome aboard Wonka Air Flight SOS-911, a non-stop Glass Elevator service from The Chocolate Factory to the Space Hotel - USA. We are currently the first in line for take-off (and most likely, we'll be the only one). We are expected to punch through the Factory's roof in approximately 5 minutes. We suggest that you keep your nightshirts, knickers, dentures, other personal belongings fastened and your emesis bags close throughout the flight</span>
  <span id="freeText16187621979243165065" style="display:none"><b>[Preflight Announcement]</b><br /><br />Good day, ladies and gentlemen! <br />Welcome aboard Wonka Air Flight SOS-911, a non-stop Glass Elevator service from The Chocolate Factory to the Space Hotel - USA. We are currently the first in line for take-off (and most likely, we'll be the only one). We are expected to punch through the Factory's roof in approximately 5 minutes. We suggest that you keep your nightshirts, knickers, dentures, other personal belongings fastened and your emesis bags close throughout the flight, as we may expect atmospheric turbulence, symptomatic migraines, and extreme motion sickness. For that, we do apologise in advance. We ask that your seats and tables (if there is one) be in their full upright-position prior take-off. Smoking is strictly prohibited inside the aircraft including the lavatories (if ever present) for the entire duration of the flight. So, hold your horses! Grab your gizzards and pray that you arrive in one piece! If there is anything we can do to make your flight more enjoyable, let us know and thank you for choosing Wonka Air! <br /><br /><b>[Captain's Announcement]</b><br /><br />Dear passengers, this is your captain speaking. First, I'd like to welcome the following people onboard Wonka Air Flight SOS-911: Charlie Bucket, Mr. and Mrs. Bucket, Grandma Josephine, Grandpa Joe, Grandma Georgina and Grandpa George. We are currently cruising at an immense altitude of 1,261,154,400 feet at an airspeed of 17,000 miles an hour. Please be reminded that I won't be able to determine the weather conditions as of this moment for we are travelling at a blinding speed, however, fear not of being roasted to a crisp or frizzled to a fritter! For our flight is <i>"air-conditioned, ventilated, aerated and automated"</i> as well as <i>"shockproof, waterproof, bombproof, bulletproof and Knidproof"</i>. Help yourselves to some scrumdiddlyumptious food as we have a non-existent cabin crew. We also don't need any in-flight movie and we are currently experiencing a horrifying one through our see-through aircraft — behold the Vermicious Knid and its victims aboard the Transport Capsule! Will they survive? That is the question! <br /><br />And now as your captain, it is my personal responsibility to ensure your safety lest we'll be lixivated by the colossal Knid! Should you decide to board this flight, be wary that this intergalactic expedition isn't what you might expect it to be. You may want to refer to other passenger's reviews about this flight. The tailwind clearly wasn't on its side and apparently lost its spark and magic halfway through its journey. Before deplaning, kindly check around your seat for any personal belongings you might have brought on board including your sanity. On behalf of Wonka Air and the entire non-existent crew, I would like to thank you for joining us on this trip. We are absolutely, definitely looking forward to seeing you again in the near future. Have a pleasant day! <br /><br /><b>[End Announcement]</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8893709062195947235">As we last seen the mighty, marvelous, wizard , Willy Wonka and his sidekick Charlie floating high in the sky, ( blue in color if you are curious, what else? ) in the stupendous... the Great Glass Elevator of the previous book, we wonder where in the world are they going?   <span id="freeText8893709062195947235" style="display:none">As we last seen the mighty, marvelous, wizard , Willy Wonka and his sidekick Charlie floating high in the sky, ( blue in color if you are curious, what else? ) in the stupendous... the Great Glass Elevator of the previous book, we wonder where in the world are they going? Not exactly there, someplace better for certain, but first, on board the magical contraption are of course...Willy...Charlie... the boy's parents Mr.and Mrs. Bucket ( not important enough to be given their proper names) and the four aged grandparents of the kid, the duo and the machine, had picked up...Still in the beloved ancient bed, pardon me, old Grandpa Joe is walking, sauntering in truth and has left his friends. Getting back to the adventure Wonka says he needs to travel to outer space and gain tremendous speed in the descent, to punch a large hole in his chocolate factory's roof in order to reenter the building, seems very extreme and a little dangerous the old, grumpy folks feel, they like the calm, peaceful atmosphere ... none here...and quite expensive I think to repair, however it's his edifice. Yet Mr. Willy Wonka makes Edison look like an amateur inventor next to him, this man or is he? Has everything needed for survival, let us continue this gentleman's escapades, he knows it all, Charlie believes...never gets nervous in a tight situation, unflappable always as they, the others scream in terror at the sight of thousands of evil Vermicious Knids trying to crush them, hundreds of miles above in Earth orbit. What you don't know what these creatures are? Shame on you, I take that back, few people do...picture a large egg with two menacing looking eyes , who later transform themselves into even bigger, uglier snakes. This ... silly... misunderstanding occurred because the people from the glass elevator wanted to be the first guests in the brand new glorious Space Hotel, these aliens from a planet millions of light- years away got there before, unwelcome though since not one is paying a dime, for accommodations, to be fair, the same applies equally, to the beings from the chocolate factory, however Mr. Wonka has plenty of money, he is definitely not a gatecrasher he says ...and will pay all expenses incurred. The real guests are being brought up by American astronauts and the hotel staff also, over 140 total, imagine the shock seeing Willy and Co. and these things floating around in unhealthy space... battling each other, now the snakes, trying to kill both groups, the new visitors, are not amused or believers for a while.. .yet will be soon...Houston thinks they the astronauts , have gone completely nuts describing the action, as the undaunted Willy Wonka fights back, additionally the old, petrified people inside the glass elevator, help if possible. I trust the heroes will get on solid ground in a short time, but this is debatable...A good sequel to the classic book , well worth the trouble to read... for the young at heart. And those a tiny bit older ...all are welcomed without a doubt too.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18269171723469459345">Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator: The Further Adventures of Charlie Bucket and Willy Wonka, Chocolate-Maker Extraordinaire, Roald Dahl <br/><br/>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator is a children's book by British author Roald Dahl. It is the sequel to Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, continuing the story of young Charlie Bucket and chocolatier Willy Wonka as they travel in the Great Glass Elevator. <br/><br/>The story picks up immediately where the previous book left off, with Charlie and his whole family ab</span>
  <span id="freeText18269171723469459345" style="display:none">Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator: The Further Adventures of Charlie Bucket and Willy Wonka, Chocolate-Maker Extraordinaire, Roald Dahl <br /><br />Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator is a children's book by British author Roald Dahl. It is the sequel to Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, continuing the story of young Charlie Bucket and chocolatier Willy Wonka as they travel in the Great Glass Elevator. <br /><br />The story picks up immediately where the previous book left off, with Charlie and his whole family aboard the flying Great Glass Elevator. The Elevator goes into orbit by accident, where Mr Wonka docks them at the U.S. Space Hotel. Shortly after their arrival, the hotel's elevators open, revealing man-eating monsters, known as Vermicious Knids, which form a letter of the word 'SCRAM'. Recognising the danger, Mr Wonka orders everybody off the Space Hotel. <br /><br />Upon the Elevator's departure, the monsters consumed some people aboard. Charlie suggests towing the shuttle back to Earth. Whereupon Willy Wonka returns the Elevator with the shuttle to Earth, the monsters are incinerated in the atmosphere. <br /><br />Mr Wonka releases the shuttle, and the Elevator then crashes down through the roof of the chocolate factory. Back in the chocolate factory, three of Charlie's grandparents refuse to leave their bed. Mr Wonka gives them a rejuvenation formula. They take much more than they need, and they each lose eighty years. 78-year-old Grandma Georgina vanishes, having become "-2". <br /><br />Charlie and Mr Wonka journey to 'Minusland', then Mr. Wonka restores her with a sprayable compound that makes people older. Grandma Georgina has become 358 years old. Using a cautious dose, the three are restored to their original age. <div id="review_194855915" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/194855915" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/194855915?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=read-with-neo">read-with-neo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer194855915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4162793455934110920">Neo's class has been reading Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, which led us to watching both versions of the film. When he learned of this sequel, he wanted us to give it a try. Not one he highly recommends, but here is a slightly updated version of my original review:<br/><br/>After the hair-raising adventure that Charlie Bucket underwent in the opening novel, Dahl is ready to entertain young readers again. When last we spoke of Charlie, he was loading his entire family into the glass elevator from his </span>
  <span id="freeText4162793455934110920" style="display:none">Neo's class has been reading Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, which led us to watching both versions of the film. When he learned of this sequel, he wanted us to give it a try. Not one he highly recommends, but here is a slightly updated version of my original review:<br /><br />After the hair-raising adventure that Charlie Bucket underwent in the opening novel, Dahl is ready to entertain young readers again. When last we spoke of Charlie, he was loading his entire family into the glass elevator from his newly-acquired chocolate factory. With Willy Wonka and Grandpa Joe helping at the controls, Charlie welcomes Mr. and Mrs. Bucket, Grandpa George, and Grandmas Josephine and Georgina into the machine before it blasted off. Heading up, up, up into the sky, Wonka explains the wonders of his machine, which can go in any direction and into any room whatsoever. Wonka is eager to show off the elevator's prowess, blasting it into space, where the group is spotted by a US rocket ship full of astronauts. Reporting back to the White House, these astronauts speak about the peculiar nature of the unidentified ship in front of them. The President of the United States is sure they are astronaut spies that cannot be trusted, even from afar. As Wonka and Charlie dock the elevator onto the International Space Hotel USA, more drama ensues when an extra-terrestrial being is seen wandering around. Knowing much about space and its inhabitants, Wonka helps protect the aforementioned US ship and the containment pod carrying workers for the hotel, before blasting back towards earth. Upon arrival back at the factory, Wonka seeks to enliven Charlie's grandparents, in hopes that they will get out of bed and help run the factory. Stubborn and old, George, Georgina, and Josephine refuse, but are subject to a product that Willy Wonka has been using inside the factory walls; a pill that can reverse the aging process. When the three greedy grandparents take matters into their own hands, Wonka must use another product, with the opposite effect, to calibrate their ages again. Just as Charlie thinks the drama might be done, there comes a special letter from Washington, with another round of adventures for everyone to enjoy. Dahl's creative juices were surely flowing and shall never be bottled as he creates more fun for the young and those who feel it in the bones.<br /><br />While not as crafty as the first Charlie Bucket story, Dahl brings readers into the fold with another outlandish tale that pushes the limits of the imagination. That said, it does clip along nicely and utilises some of the minor characters from the opening tale (grandparents) in a more hands-on role, which is sure to pique the interest of the reader. Dahl chooses to focus more on the action-adventure in this book than the slowly evolving adventure that touches the heart, which I did not care for as much, but still remain happy to see how things developed. The novel poses fewer themes and lessons than pure, silly entertainment for the reader. I can see what this was never picked up for a movie (to the best of my knowledge), but can only hope that if it is, Johnny Depp is kept away from the project, as he left a new generation with a sour taste in their mouths that no Oompa Loompa could fix. While the ending does leave room for more adventures and the characters could make for an interesting mix within the factory walls, the passing of Roald Dahl in 1990 has made that a natural impossibility. But, with a score of other novels for children to explore, there is hope that the new generation will look back to what entertained their parents and grandparents, finding richness in stores that did not require vampires, wizards, or even Middle School.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Dahl for touching so many lives across the generations with simple ideas that flourish into magic.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4162793455934110920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3284868291?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780425287835" href="/book/show/28186306-charlie-and-the-great-glass-elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=at-home-reading">at-home-reading</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=read-with-kids">read-with-kids</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3284868291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3621600257833090344">When I read this as a kid: 5 Stars<br/>Reread as an adult: 2 Stars<br/><br/>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory is a classic. I enjoyed it as a kid and I enjoyed it as an adult when I reread it with my kids a few months ago. Next logical step was to reread the sequel to my kids which was another book that I had fond memories of from my childhood.<br/><br/>However, this book has not aged well . . .<br/><br/>Generally, I really enjoy Dahl’s work, but I may have found one that might be best left skipped. I guess the incoherent goofine</span>
  <span id="freeText3621600257833090344" style="display:none">When I read this as a kid: 5 Stars<br />Reread as an adult: 2 Stars<br /><br />Charlie and the Chocolate Factory is a classic. I enjoyed it as a kid and I enjoyed it as an adult when I reread it with my kids a few months ago. Next logical step was to reread the sequel to my kids which was another book that I had fond memories of from my childhood.<br /><br />However, this book has not aged well . . .<br /><br />Generally, I really enjoy Dahl’s work, but I may have found one that might be best left skipped. I guess the incoherent goofiness of this was endearing to me as a child, but it was quite painful during the reread. My wife kept trying to get out of listening to it with me and the kids because it was so bad, but the kids would not let me proceed unless she was in the room! The first half of the book is a bizarre space adventure with cringe-worthy dialogue. The second half is a thinly veiled commentary on drug overdosing – including an <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oompa Loompa song about a girl ODing on laxatives and having permanent damage where she must sit on the toilet for hours every day <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It’s just makes me wonder a lot about where this all came from after the wonderful first book.<br /><br />Also, there are many cultural representations in this book that would not fly today. Some of you have seen on Disney+ where they have left the old movies in tact but put a warning on movies like Dumbo and Peter Pan that they contain dated cultural references – this book needs that disclaimer! As racial tensions have been very high in the news lately, know that this book would not hold up in the debate. This is especially troublesome as it is geared towards children – so I kind of skimmed a few parts. Maybe back when it was written it was not a big deal, but there are several things here I would not want my kids repeating in public!<br /><br />So, approach this one with caution. If you want to complete Charlie and Willy Wonka’s journey, then give it a go and maybe you will enjoy it more than I did. But, you have been warned about what you are getting into!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3621600257833090344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_302906688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302906688" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8108251-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333400859p2/8108251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302906688?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/8108251-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8108251-anthony?shelf=juvenile-fiction">juvenile-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302906688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9000315128403609914">“Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator” picks up where “Charlie and the Chocolate Factory” left of, but if “’Charlie and the Chocolate Factory’ is Dahl at his best…” then “Charlie and the great Glass Elevator is Dahl at his worst. However, children will still love the silliness of it all.<br/><br/>The best way to describe “…the Great Glass Elevator” is clumsy and inane. The Big differences between “Chocolate Factory” and “…Glass Elevator” is that former is silly with a point and congruent within itself, an</span>
  <span id="freeText9000315128403609914" style="display:none">“Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator” picks up where “Charlie and the Chocolate Factory” left of, but if “’Charlie and the Chocolate Factory’ is Dahl at his best…” then “Charlie and the great Glass Elevator is Dahl at his worst. However, children will still love the silliness of it all.<br /><br />The best way to describe “…the Great Glass Elevator” is clumsy and inane. The Big differences between “Chocolate Factory” and “…Glass Elevator” is that former is silly with a point and congruent within itself, and the latter is pointlessly silly and seems full of discrepancies. In “…Chocolate Factory” there was a clearly developed plot and moral in amongst all that silliness, but in “…Glass Elevator” I have no idea why it went the way it did. And even though this is supposed to be a sequel, I could be wrong but there seems to be a discrepancy in the age of the grandparents. In addition the story often doesn’t seem to jive with itself. Of course there is always the giant possibility that I was so utterly bored with this book that I didn’t catch everything. <br /><br />Needless to say, young children, for whom this book was intended, will probably enjoy the silly imagination of this story, but adults like me probably won’t like it so much. I think I probably wanted more chocolate factory and less outer space nonsense. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9000315128403609914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333049751?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333049751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12513453225315415869">I just discovered <i>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator</i> was written the year I was born. Apparently a lot of my favorite childhood kids' books were written that year. 1972 seemed to be the year of the fanciful, magical and/or pastoral, nature-oriented kids' book: <i>Watership Down, All Creatures Great and Small, Tales of a Fourth Grade Nothing, Frog and Toad #2, Earthsea Cycle #3</i>.<br/><br/>This might explain a few things about me...but then again it more likely has a whole lot more to say about where the Amer</span>
  <span id="freeText12513453225315415869" style="display:none">I just discovered <i>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator</i> was written the year I was born. Apparently a lot of my favorite childhood kids' books were written that year. 1972 seemed to be the year of the fanciful, magical and/or pastoral, nature-oriented kids' book: <i>Watership Down, All Creatures Great and Small, Tales of a Fourth Grade Nothing, Frog and Toad #2, Earthsea Cycle #3</i>.<br /><br />This might explain a few things about me...but then again it more likely has a whole lot more to say about where the American reading public's mind was at the time: fully ensconced in Vietnam and sick of it. It was time for a bit of escapism and Roald Dahl's books provided just that.<br /><br />This is a sequel of <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i> which picks up right were its predecessor left off, at least story-wise. It does not however pick up and carry on the same level of fantastical fun and frivolity. Remember feeling underwhelmed, not quite as carried away with this one as I did the first (Ironic, considering it takes place in a flying elevator). Perhaps it's because the shine has worn off a bit, the surprises have been sprung and now that the reader knows what to expect in Wonka it all doesn't seem quite as magical. Oh well. Just the same, it's still a fun-as-heck book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12513453225315415869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bookshelf">bookshelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1598953114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16065829440222348549">Unlike it's predecessor, <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, this book is probably a bit too far-fetched for it to grab the same amount of attention. It's an odd little book-it has some good moments and is written much in the same way as the first book-and his many others-but it definitely has it's faults.<br/><br/>Of-the-time-racism was probably the biggest one. It's difficult to critique something that was "okay" at the time of the book being published, but I can't help but think that perhaps that, along</span>
  <span id="freeText16065829440222348549" style="display:none">Unlike it's predecessor, <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, this book is probably a bit too far-fetched for it to grab the same amount of attention. It's an odd little book-it has some good moments and is written much in the same way as the first book-and his many others-but it definitely has it's faults.<br /><br />Of-the-time-racism was probably the biggest one. It's difficult to critique something that was "okay" at the time of the book being published, but I can't help but think that perhaps that, along with the quite-too-much-whimsy storyline has contributed to this one being almost forgotten. There is still some great imagination, but there just seemed to be something completely lacking: possibly the very flimsy and thin plot and the rather annoying characters of Charlie's bed-ridden grandparents.<br /><br />It was, however, mercifully short and a nice quick read that took me away from the heavy and serious Classics for a while, which is always great. I'm sure children will enjoy it immensely, though I'd perhaps be a bit vigilante when it comes to the jokes about the Chinese.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk/blogs/infinite-variety-books" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/infiniteANDdarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/infinitedarlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://uk.pinterest.com/infinitedarling/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://www.infiniteanddarling.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Shop</a> | <a href="https://www.etsy.com/uk/shop/infiniteANDdarling" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<div id="review_1888177875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1888177875" />
    <a title="Mariah Roze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze"><img alt="Mariah Roze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496763524p2/22371819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888177875?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariah Roze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariah Roze" href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze">Mariah Roze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141365381" href="/book/show/29093192-charlie-and-the-great-glass-elevator">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariah Roze by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888177875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13644322518836790486">I am currently trying to read through all of Roald Dahl's books because growing up I loved the ones that I read. I originally read Charlie and the Chocolate factory when I was in middle school. I thought it was about time to finally read the second book.<br/><br/>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator was a very interesting book. It was not what I expected (for the first half of the book) and I was very disappointed by that. I felt like this book was two short stories combined. More than half of the book ta</span>
  <span id="freeText13644322518836790486" style="display:none">I am currently trying to read through all of Roald Dahl's books because growing up I loved the ones that I read. I originally read Charlie and the Chocolate factory when I was in middle school. I thought it was about time to finally read the second book.<br /><br />Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator was a very interesting book. It was not what I expected (for the first half of the book) and I was very disappointed by that. I felt like this book was two short stories combined. More than half of the book takes place in space and in an elevator. It has nothing to do with the Chocolate Factory at all. It felt like Roald Dahl used Charlie, his family and Willie Wanka as the characters in that "short story" because he didn't want to have to create background information on new people.<br /><br />Then for the second half of the book they go back to the Factory and the Umpa Lumpas sang multiple songs. Nothing else that happened really had anything to do with the factory. The grandparents were affected by some of the candy, but that could have taken place anywhere.<br /><br />This book was a much let down compared to the first book. The only reason it received 3 stars from me is because Roald Dahl is an amazing writer and can even make the worst books extremely readable and somewhat entertaining. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13644322518836790486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135267299" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135267299" />
    <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again"><img alt="Jeanette (Again)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304653755p2/796425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135267299?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette (Again)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette (Again)" href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-again">Jeanette (Again)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780394924724" href="/book/show/1105406.Charlie_and_the_Great_Glass_Elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=books-little-me-loved">books-little-me-loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=for-the-munchkins">for-the-munchkins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=all-fiction">all-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=just-plain-bizarre">just-plain-bizarre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-again?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135267299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14450209745513871593">I remember as a kid being quite disappointed by this book, having so thoroughly loved Charlie and the Chocolate Factory. Now I can see why I wasn't that thrilled with this second one. I wasn't into anything smacking of sci-fi or space travel as a kid. There were probably a few exceptions, but I mostly steered clear of those books. <br/><br/>This book is weird. It's almost two books merged into one. The first 92 pages or so is somewhat of a Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy for kids. It's that weird and off</span>
  <span id="freeText14450209745513871593" style="display:none">I remember as a kid being quite disappointed by this book, having so thoroughly loved Charlie and the Chocolate Factory. Now I can see why I wasn't that thrilled with this second one. I wasn't into anything smacking of sci-fi or space travel as a kid. There were probably a few exceptions, but I mostly steered clear of those books. <br /><br />This book is weird. It's almost two books merged into one. The first 92 pages or so is somewhat of a Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy for kids. It's that weird and off the wall, with the same kind of matter-of-fact absurdity. Willy Wonka could stand in for Zaphod Beeblebrox, Charlie would be Arthur Dent, and Grandmas Josephine and Georgina could co-star as Marvin the pessimistic robot. I don't know who would be Ford Prefect, though. Maybe Grandpa Joe? <br /><br />The rest of the book after they crash back into the Chocolate Factory is a completely different story about pills Willy Wonka has invented that can add to or subtract from your age. It's all very clever, but it lacks the charm and magic of the first book. At the end when Dahl brings the two story lines back together, it seems like an afterthought, like an "oops, better tie everything together and end this thing." <br /><br />There are some very funny moments in the book, most having to do with word play, but they seem to be written for grown-ups rather than for children. The humor and subtext is just too subtle for kids. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14450209745513871593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_557878518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/557878518" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1661541-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591375875p2/1661541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/557878518?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/1661541-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141301129" href="/book/show/385247.Charlie_and_the_Great_Glass_Elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=in-classroom">in-classroom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=vps">vps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=dahl">dahl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=4-9">4-9</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1661541-robert?shelf=space">space</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer557878518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2159172532110195667">This is the sequel to <u>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</u>. My heavens, this was not good. This is the only Dahl book I have read to date that did not interest me in the least. It was contrived . . . and contrived badly.<br/><br/>The first half of the book placed our hero and Mr. Wonka in space. Yes, it was a bad Miss Frizzle episode. Horrid, I say. The premise of that part was that the elevator had gone into orbit accidentally and they had no control over returning. After bouncing around with knids and othe</span>
  <span id="freeText2159172532110195667" style="display:none">This is the sequel to <u>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</u>. My heavens, this was not good. This is the only Dahl book I have read to date that did not interest me in the least. It was contrived . . . and contrived badly.<br /><br />The first half of the book placed our hero and Mr. Wonka in space. Yes, it was a bad Miss Frizzle episode. Horrid, I say. The premise of that part was that the elevator had gone into orbit accidentally and they had no control over returning. After bouncing around with knids and other things that go bump in the night sky, all of a sudden the elevator was capable of re-entering the atmosphere and was able to tow a spaceship with it. Remarkable!<br /><br />The second half of the book was marginally better. The crew returned to the chocolate factory. Unlike the original text, this was completely boring. Too old, too young, too old, just right. Bah!<br /><br />This is a daffy, half-assed attempt at continuing a fabulous story. Did you ever see Grease II? It was even worse than that!<br /><br />I've read that Dahl began a third installment where the cast headed off to the White House but only completed a single chapter. I think his readers were lucky with that. Really, what is the motivation of a young English boy who now owns a marvelous chocolate factory to go to America and take in a dotty president as depicted here?<br /><br />A waste of my time reading this. And to think, I am a Dahl fan! Ha!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2159172532110195667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3032881949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3032881949" />
    <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews"><img alt="Briar&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402183274p2/32054036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3032881949?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=other-editions">other-editions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fun">fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3032881949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11737753321657340632">This book was the weirdest sequel I've ever read, if I'm being honest.<br/><br/>I truly expected some more crazy chocolate factory action, but involving a glass elevator. Welp, I hope you wanted Charlie, Willy and Grandpa Joe heading to space and a dumb American government, because that's whatcha got.<br/><br/>I will say that Roald Dahl is a marvelous writer and a lot of this book is amusing! He's got a unique style that made me laugh as an adult but also see how a child could love this book just as much. At the sa</span>
  <span id="freeText11737753321657340632" style="display:none">This book was the weirdest sequel I've ever read, if I'm being honest.<br /><br />I truly expected some more crazy chocolate factory action, but involving a glass elevator. Welp, I hope you wanted Charlie, Willy and Grandpa Joe heading to space and a dumb American government, because that's whatcha got.<br /><br />I will say that Roald Dahl is a marvelous writer and a lot of this book is amusing! He's got a unique style that made me laugh as an adult but also see how a child could love this book just as much. At the same time, this book wasn't as interesting to me. The big adventure was really cool and seemed totally "out of this world" (pun intended) but it didn't feel as fun as the first book. There's no way I would have been able to guess the ending to this book.<br /><br />In that regards, that's probably why it makes such a fun kids book. Kids love adventure, fun and comedy so they'll really dig this book. As an adult, I'd rather read it my kids or reading buddies instead of enjoying it myself. I want to finish off this series and read more by Roald Dahl because of his pure genius. <br /><br />Alas, it's still a classic and beautifully written. I'd highly recommend it as a children's novel or if you love a good classic book. <br /><br />Two out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11737753321657340632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2205708323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2205708323" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9199123501468501601">Another reviewer has said that “if Charlie and the Chocolate Factory is Dahl at his best, then Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator is Dahl at his worst.” Objectively, I would have to quite agree. This strange sequel about Charlie, Willy Wonka, Mr. Bucket, Mrs. Bucket, and the four grandparents accidentally going too far in the elevator, ending up in outer-space, being mistaken for terrorists by the US Government, and avoiding man-eating aliens had me thoroughly scratching my head. It’s a sequel</span>
  <span id="freeText9199123501468501601" style="display:none">Another reviewer has said that “if Charlie and the Chocolate Factory is Dahl at his best, then Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator is Dahl at his worst.” Objectively, I would have to quite agree. This strange sequel about Charlie, Willy Wonka, Mr. Bucket, Mrs. Bucket, and the four grandparents accidentally going too far in the elevator, ending up in outer-space, being mistaken for terrorists by the US Government, and avoiding man-eating aliens had me thoroughly scratching my head. It’s a sequel that lacks all the magical charm of its predecessor. The work feels uninspired—as if Dahl had written it in mocking response to his publisher's pressure to write a sequel for his most popular book. But you know what? <br /> <br />I enjoyed it for this ludicrous, acid-trip of a story that it was.</span>

<div id="review_3253933866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3253933866" />
    <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma"><img alt="Nandakishore Varma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583648733p2/6237864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3253933866?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141322698" href="/book/show/1154730.Charlie_and_the_Great_Glass_Elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3253933866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9197908625610761573"><b>Warning: Mild spoliers</b><br/><br/>Authors should know when to stop. This sequel should never have been written. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_' title='Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a>, Roald Dahl had a terrific concept and a nice story - here he has neither. We read it only because the author has a nice way with words, and we love Willie Wonka and Charlie already.<br/><br/>If you have read the first book in the series (otherwise, what are you doing, reading this review?) you'd know that it ends with the whole Bucket family (two sets of grandparents, M</span>
  <span id="freeText9197908625610761573" style="display:none"><b>Warning: Mild spoliers</b><br /><br />Authors should know when to stop. This sequel should never have been written. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_" title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a>, Roald Dahl had a terrific concept and a nice story - here he has neither. We read it only because the author has a nice way with words, and we love Willie Wonka and Charlie already.<br /><br />If you have read the first book in the series (otherwise, what are you doing, reading this review?) you'd know that it ends with the whole Bucket family (two sets of grandparents, Mrs. and Mr. Bucket, and Charlie) and Willy Wonka shooting off to his factory in his glass lift (which can do many wondrous things). Well, it does not reach there. Due to the shenanigans of one grandparent, it shoots off into orbit. There it meets "Space Hotel U.S.A", the first ever hotel in outer space, officially launched by Good Ol' Murrica. And just when we thought we had a story, things start to unravel. The thread goes all over the place like a spilled bowl of spaghetti.<br /><br />We meet the "Vermicious Knids", nasty monsters from outer space; A moronic U. S. President and his wacky cabinet; and Willy Wonka's wondrous chocolates which can increase and decrease people's age miraculously. We make a trip to Minusland where the people who regress too much into their youth go to. The story flows on haphazardly till it comes to a totally contrived end which hints at another book in the series (which was attempted, but thankfully, given up after the first chapter by Dahl.)<br /><br />I wouldn't call the book a total loss, however. The dumb President Lancelot R. Gilligrass, the Vice President Miss Tibbs who is also his nanny and the real power in the White House, the sword-swallower from Afghanistan who is teaching the president to swallow his words, the Financial Adviser who has great trouble balancing the budget on his head, the trigger-happy army chief who likes to blow things up... this whole team was hilarious! (I know what you are thinking - but no, this was written in 1973.) And the names of the Russian President (Yougetoff) and the Chinese Premier and Assistant Premier (How-Yu-Bin and Chu-On-Dat, respectively) are worthy of Goscinny and Uderzo. I would have liked to learn more about these wonderful people, than the done-to-death chocolate factory.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9197908625610761573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer41843970486104099">Part of my personal reading challenge (reading through the New York Public Library's "Top 100 Kids' Books). Like <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>The Great Glass Elevator</i> was whacky and zany. But I personally had more fun with the first one. While the chocolate factory was magical, this book spent a lot time zooming through space with Charlie's insufferable grandparents that are too lazy to get out of bed. But the last third of the book is spent on getting his insufferably greedy grandparents </span>
  <span id="freeText41843970486104099" style="display:none">Part of my personal reading challenge (reading through the New York Public Library's "Top 100 Kids' Books). Like <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>The Great Glass Elevator</i> was whacky and zany. But I personally had more fun with the first one. While the chocolate factory was magical, this book spent a lot time zooming through space with Charlie's insufferable grandparents that are too lazy to get out of bed. But the last third of the book is spent on getting his insufferably greedy grandparents back to their proper age when they take too much youth medicine to change their age. <br /><br />Still classic Dahl. Still fun. But not as fun as exploring the magical world of the factory. <br /><br />I'd rate this book a G.</span>

<div id="review_3082913279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3082913279" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3082913279?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0141371366" href="/book/show/44436754-charlie-and-the-great-glass-elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3082913279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10788108253373244475"><b>Pretty Silly</b><br/>15 December 2019<br/><br/>	You know when an author writes a book that becomes so popular that they make a movie out of it, and the movie also becomes an absolute classic as well. Well, this isn’t that book, this is the sequal to that book, and needless to say that this book blows, and it blows incredibly hard. I guess there is a really good reason why they never actually made a movie out of this book, and stared Gene Wilder in it either.<br/><br/>	Honestly, it is actually one of those books that I would</span>
  <span id="freeText10788108253373244475" style="display:none"><b>Pretty Silly</b><br />15 December 2019<br /><br />	You know when an author writes a book that becomes so popular that they make a movie out of it, and the movie also becomes an absolute classic as well. Well, this isn’t that book, this is the sequal to that book, and needless to say that this book blows, and it blows incredibly hard. I guess there is a really good reason why they never actually made a movie out of this book, and stared Gene Wilder in it either.<br /><br />	Honestly, it is actually one of those books that I would rather just forget and a part of me wonders why I even bothered to get my hands on it and read it. Actually, that is a pretty stupid question because I know the answer – I remember reading it a really long time ago, and I didn’t want to write a review without actually giving the book another chance. Well, the fact that the first book is a classic lead me to believe that this book is the same.<br /><br />	Well, you could say that in this book they end up in orbit after playing around with the elevator, and while they are in orbit they discover that the universe is ruled by these vicious monsters that pretty much destroy anything that attempts to leave Earth’s atmosphere, but they can’t land on Earth because they burn up on reentry. Oh, and they also end up on a space station, and start playing games with the Amercian President, whose Nanny happens to be his Vice-President (my eyes honestly rolled at that concept).<br /><br />	Mind you, some people claim that we have a man-boy currently in the White House, though I would hardly suggest that the current VP would come anywhere close to being his Nanny (and I suspect that maybe he wouldn’t listen to her anyway even if he happened to have one). Still, this isn’t a political commentary, though one might suggest that Dahl was quite insightful at times where he suggests that the Vice President actually turns out to be much more influential than the actual president, and the president that ends up getting elected is, well, just a figure head.<br /><br />	Then the second half of the book has them return to the chocolate factory and some disaster over anti-aging drugs that Wonka has discovered (in fact they are drugs that basically reduce your age by something like 20 years, and in a rush to become younger, Charlie’s grandparents end up scoffing a head of them). Yeah, as I said, this book ended up being pretty silly, and in fact, it was bordering on nonsense. Sure, there are people that are likely to protest, but in the end, I would recommend passing on this book – just stick with the first one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10788108253373244475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3022086268" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3022086268" />
    <a title="Noriko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30787873-noriko"><img alt="Noriko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590582709p2/30787873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3022086268?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noriko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noriko" href="/user/show/30787873-noriko">Noriko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18876348-charlie-and-the-great-glass-elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30787873-noriko?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30787873-noriko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30787873-noriko?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3022086268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6835622660584550727">Wow Wow Wow Wow WOW. What the heck did I just read? <br/><b>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator</b>, the sequel to the famous <em>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</em> literally blew my mind in a different way, and I quite enjoyed this awfully far-fetched yet a glorious journey!<br/><br/>The story picks up at exactly where we left off in the previous book. I must admit that the ending of the first book was rather abrupt as though it was chopped off undeveloped, but no sooner had I started reading this book than I figured ou</span>
  <span id="freeText6835622660584550727" style="display:none">Wow Wow Wow Wow WOW. What the heck did I just read? <br /><b>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator</b>, the sequel to the famous <em>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</em> literally blew my mind in a different way, and I quite enjoyed this awfully far-fetched yet a glorious journey!<br /><br />The story picks up at exactly where we left off in the previous book. I must admit that the ending of the first book was rather abrupt as though it was chopped off undeveloped, but no sooner had I started reading this book than I figured out the reason why. My niggle toward the previous book instantly disappeared and the literally out of the world, super weird story and hilarious banter among the Bucket Grandmas and Mr. Wonka pulled me into the story right off the bat. <br /><br />Then the story expands EVEN MORE and of all places, it launches into SPACE! Would I never, ever, have imagined this development?? <br />Just like the previous book, Dahl's writing peppered with wit and hilarity and Quentin Blake's scintillating, vibrant illustration captivated me the entire time. <br />To be perfectly honest, the whole Vermicious Knids episode was the point where Dahl could have gone a bit too far and I almost lost my interest, but once the characters are safely brought back down to earth, I got drawn in the story again. <br /><br />One thing I can say about this book is, well, obviously there's no end to Roald Dahl's creativity and imagination. The plot is as subversive as the previous book and the contrast of light and dark is striking as ever, yet Dahl managed to maintain the perfect balance, keeping the story from derailing completely. This book might be a hit or miss depending on a reader (because it's a bit too far-fetched and over the top), but I think this book is a first-class slapstick and managed to tie everything together without leaving many loose ends. <br /><br />All in all, <b>Charlie and the Great Glass Elevator </b>is as fantastical and imaginative a story as the previous one, and I am quite glad that I finally read this sequel. It's kind of sad there's no more sequels to this series and have to say goodbye to my favorite characters, but I will come back to this hysterically funny story every now and then for sure!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6835622660584550727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904836476?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/12555370-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11082471-charlie-and-the-great-glass-elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12555370-jason?shelf=read-to-cass">read-to-cass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12555370-jason?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904836476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8383291328902329213">Ahhhhh! that age old problem of sequels, they are never as good as the original story, not even Roald Dahl is able to break that problem.<br/><br/>In the great glass elevator Dahl attempts to write a Sci-Fi story, I think it is the first time he has done that and for me his story telling doesn't work as well up in space. Down on Earth you can believe in giants and chocolate factories using slave labour and also a kid travelling on a flying giant peach, because all of that is just fantasy. But once you sta</span>
  <span id="freeText8383291328902329213" style="display:none">Ahhhhh! that age old problem of sequels, they are never as good as the original story, not even Roald Dahl is able to break that problem.<br /><br />In the great glass elevator Dahl attempts to write a Sci-Fi story, I think it is the first time he has done that and for me his story telling doesn't work as well up in space. Down on Earth you can believe in giants and chocolate factories using slave labour and also a kid travelling on a flying giant peach, because all of that is just fantasy. But once you start bringing Sci-Fi into the story you have to make things a bit more believable and Dahl doesn't do that. This breaks the magic and you realise just how annoying his characters are and how silly the plot is....honestly, imagine America voting in a silly, immature President. <br /><br />Still, Dahl has written so many amazing stories I'm sure he is allowed one hiccup.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8383291328902329213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/16092014-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140328707" href="/book/show/1910094.Charlie_and_the_Great_Glass_Elevator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16092014-paul?shelf=kiddos">kiddos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16092014-paul?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837663668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3342779627382199844">This was a bedtime readaloud to the kiddos, and frankly, if they hadn't been enjoying it so much, I wouldn't have finished it. All three said they enjoyed it better than <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory,</i> so we had a good hour-long conversation about the perils of recency bias. Kidding. But really, this book is not great. I remember enjoying it as a kid, but adults beware: the plot is a mess, the jokes fall flat (especially the borderline-racist ones), and despite some good moments, the overall </span>
  <span id="freeText3342779627382199844" style="display:none">This was a bedtime readaloud to the kiddos, and frankly, if they hadn't been enjoying it so much, I wouldn't have finished it. All three said they enjoyed it better than <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory,</i> so we had a good hour-long conversation about the perils of recency bias. Kidding. But really, this book is not great. I remember enjoying it as a kid, but adults beware: the plot is a mess, the jokes fall flat (especially the borderline-racist ones), and despite some good moments, the overall impression is that Dahl was more interested in capitalizing off the success of Willy Wonka than telling any kind of a coherent story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3342779627382199844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2565770243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11781581735305454324">Not as great as the first part, but still enjoyable. I have a feeling, I might add Roald Dahl to my 'to read everything I can get my hands on' list. The storytelling (as absurd as it gets) is really indulging. I know I would have loved this if I read it when I was a child, and well, I'm liking it as an adult as well. That speaks for itself.</span>

          </span>
